# ðŸ“‹ **ISO 11135 Professional Regulatory Compliance Guide**
*Comprehensive Ethylene Oxide Sterilization Requirements & Guidelines*

**Document Source**: ISO 11135:2014+A1:2019 - Sterilization of health care products â€” Ethylene oxide  
**Total Parameter Categories**: 10  
**Total Requirements**: 849

## ðŸ”¹ **Product Requirement Compliance Requirements**

**Product Requirements for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization - Compliance with ISO 11135**
**Introduction**
The product requirements outlined in this document are essential for ensuring compliance with the International Organization for Standardization (ISO) standard, BS EN ISO 11135:2014+A1:2019. These requirements apply to all products undergoing ethylene oxide sterilization and must be met to ensure the safety and efficacy of the final product.
**Temperature Requirements**
The equipment used for ethylene oxide sterilization shall have temperature monitoring capabilities that include:
- Airflow detection equipment, alarm systems or indicators to monitor the air handling system and ensure it operates within predetermined tolerances.
- Equipment to re-circulate air.
- Means of monitoring room temperature.
- Means of controlling room temperature.
The equipment specification shall be reviewed to ensure compliance with regulatory and safety requirements, technical specifications are appropriate, and services and infrastructure necessary to operate the equipment are available.
**Thermal Requirements**
Effluent gas from the ethylene oxide sterilization process shall be discharged through an EO gas treatment system, such as a catalytic oxidizer, wet acid scrubber or thermal oxidizer, in compliance with local permit requirements or emission control legislation. When choosing a diluent, consideration should be given to its ozone depleting potential and disposal of any by-products.
**Heat Requirements**
Products shall be designed to allow removal of air, if applicable, and penetration of heat, humidity and ethylene oxide during the sterilization process, and removal of ethylene oxide at the end of the process. Packaging shall also be designed to meet these requirements.
The load configuration shall ensure that products are exposed to a uniform distribution of heat, humidity and ethylene oxide throughout the sterilization cycle.
**Validation Requirements**
When introducing new or modified products into an existing ethylene oxide sterilization process, a validation study shall be performed to demonstrate equivalence. This includes:
- Comparison with the validated product and/or Process Control Document (PCD) used to validate the existing EO process.
- Examination of factors that could affect the initial bioburden on the product, including manufacturing facilities, raw materials, sources of these materials and production processes.
The validation study shall include evidence or assessment of the bioburden of the product and its resistance relative to the internal PCD. A documented conclusion shall be made that the new or modified product is suitable for adoption into the product family/processing category specifically referenced in the current validation study, achieving the specified Sterilization Assurance Level (SAL).
**Documentation Requirements**
The following documentation shall be maintained:
- Evidence of validation studies performed on products and equipment.
- Documentation of any additional tests performed to supplement existing validation studies.
- Results from residual testing, functional testing on first three lots, etc.
**Approval Requirements**
Approval by the sterilization specialist and other individuals as required by the organization's quality management system shall be obtained before releasing new or modified products into production.
By meeting these product requirements, organizations can ensure compliance with ISO 11135 and provide safe and effective ethylene oxide sterilized products to their customers.
To ensure the effectiveness and safety of ethylene oxide sterilization, manufacturers must comply with the requirements outlined in ISO 11135. This standard provides a framework for validating the sterilization process and ensuring that products are properly processed to achieve the required Sterility Assurance Level (SAL). The following guidance outlines the product requirements for compliance with ISO 11135.
**Product Definition**
The manufacturer of the device shall document the results of product definition, which includes establishing the sterilization process applicable for the defined product. This involves:
* Establishing a process specification that can be applied for the sterilization of the defined product during validation studies (Clause 8).
* Defining the sterilization process applicable for the defined product, including new or modified products, packaging, or loading configurations (Clause 8.2).
**Process Definition**
The purpose of process definition is to obtain a process specification that can be applied for the sterilization of the defined product during validation studies (Clause 8). This involves:
* Performing process definition activities in a sterilization chamber (developmental chamber or production chamber) (Clause 8.3).
* Establishing the sterilization process applicable for the defined product, including new or modified products, packaging, or loading configurations (Clause 8.2).
**Validation**
The purpose of validation is to demonstrate that the sterilization process established in the process definition can be delivered effectively and reproducibly to the product within the sterilization load (Clause 9). Validation consists of a number of identified stages:
* Process qualification: demonstrating that the specified sterilization process is effective in sterilizing the most difficult-to-sterilize location within the product (Clause 7.1.6).
* Product validation: demonstrating that the sterilization process can be delivered effectively and reproducibly to the product within the sterilization load.
**Sterility Assurance Level (SAL)**
The required SAL shall be achieved through the demonstration of equivalence to a previously validated product, or internal process challenge device (internal PCD) used to qualify the product SAL when exposed to the specified sterilization process (Clause 7.1.6).
**Product Family**
A product family is a collection of products determined to be similar or equivalent for validation purposes. Although product families can be used for other reasons, for EO sterilization, a product family usually refers to products that have been grouped together for the purposes of determining that the required SAL has been delivered to the product.
**Single Batch Release**
Single batch release data can be generated under either a stand-alone protocol for release of that batch or as one part of a full validation. This approach shall only be used to release product to market from multiple batches if it is part of a full validation.
**Compliance Requirements**
To ensure compliance with ISO 11135, manufacturers must:
* Document the results of product definition (Clause 7.4).
* Establish a process specification that can be applied for the sterilization of the defined product during validation studies (Clause 8).
* Perform process definition activities in a sterilization chamber (developmental chamber or production chamber) (Clause 8.3).
* Demonstrate that the specified sterilization process is effective in sterilizing the most difficult-to-sterilize location within the product (Clause 7.1.6).
* Achieve the required SAL through the demonstration of equivalence to a previously validated product, or internal PCD used to qualify the product SAL when exposed to the specified sterilization process (Clause 7.1.6).
**Audit Readiness**
Manufacturers must maintain records and documentation to demonstrate compliance with ISO 11135 requirements. This includes:
* Product definition documentation.
* Process definition documentation.
* Validation documentation, including process qualification and product validation.
* Sterility Assurance Level (SAL) documentation.
By following the guidelines outlined in this document, manufacturers can ensure that their products are properly sterilized and meet the required standards for compliance with ISO 11135.
The requirements outlined in this document are essential for ensuring the sterilization of medical devices using ethylene oxide (EO) gas. Adherence to these product requirements is crucial for maintaining compliance with the International Organization for Standardization (ISO) 11135 standard.
**Product Family and Processing Category**
1. **Assessment of Packaged Product**
   The packaged product shall be assessed to determine if it can be assigned to an existing product family for sterilization purposes. This assessment considers:
      a) Product composition
      b) Design
      c) Any other relevant factors
2. **Product Qualification**
   A product qualification study is required when:
      a) The product differs significantly in density from that of the reference load;
      b) The product differs significantly in total load volume;
      c) The presence of either occluded spaces or mated surfaces requires evaluation for internal Product Control Devices (PCDs);
      d) Changes to the sterilization process may affect product sterility.
3. **Product Equivalence**
   A review shall be conducted to determine whether a candidate product or packaging system can be adopted into a product family or processing category. This review considers:
      a) The resistance of the Product Control Device (PCD) to EO;
      b) The bioburden level of the product as presented for sterilization.
**Microbial Resistance**
1. **EO Sterilization Process**
   The resistance of the PCD to EO shall be shown to be equal to or greater than the resistance of the bioburden of product to be sterilized at the most difficult to sterilize location on the product.
2. **Bioburden Level**
   The bioburden level of the product as presented for sterilization may be affected by:
      a) Increased distances between manufacturing facility and sterilization site;
      b) Differences in manufacturing environments.
**Monitoring and Control**
1. **Software Validation**
   Software used to control and/or monitor the process shall be prepared and validated in accordance with a quality system that provides documented evidence that the software meets its design specification.
2. **Process Variables**
   The means of monitoring and controlling process variables shall be determined and specified.
3. **Control Function Failure**
   Means shall be provided to ensure that failure in a control function does not lead to failure in recording of process variables, such that an ineffective process appears effective.
**Compliance Importance**
Adherence to these product requirements is essential for maintaining compliance with the ISO 11135 standard and ensuring the sterilization of medical devices using ethylene oxide gas. Failure to comply may result in non-sterile products being released to market, which can have serious consequences for patient safety and regulatory compliance.
This document provides comprehensive guidance on product requirements for ethylene oxide sterilization. It is essential that organizations implementing these requirements maintain accurate records of validation, qualification, and monitoring activities to ensure audit readiness.
To ensure the effective sterilization of medical devices, it is essential to comply with the product requirements outlined in ISO 11135. This document provides a comprehensive guide to the product requirements necessary for ethylene oxide sterilization.
**Product Definition (7.1)**
The purpose of this activity is to define the product to be sterilized, including its microbiological quality prior to sterilization. The following information shall be documented:
* Product description
* Microbiological quality of the product prior to sterilization
* Any specific requirements for the product, such as temperature or humidity control
**Product Realization (D.4.3)**
The requirements for product realization relate to the product lifecycle from determination of customer requirements, design and development, purchasing, control of production, and calibration of monitoring and measuring devices.
* The following shall be considered:
	+ Determination of customer requirements
	+ Design and development of the product
	+ Purchasing of materials or services that impact process quality
	+ Control of production to ensure consistency and quality
	+ Calibration of monitoring and measuring devices
**Performance and Monitoring Capabilities (D.6.3)**
The following equipment shall be used to monitor and control the sterilization process:
* Airflow detection equipment, alarm systems or indicators to ensure that the air handling system operates within predetermined tolerances and maintains adequate airflow in a loaded room or chamber
* Equipment to re-circulate air
* Means of monitoring room temperature
* Means of controlling room temperature
**Redundant Sensors (D.6.3.5)**
To prevent undetected failure of control or monitoring functions, redundant sensors shall be used for many critical process parameters.
* The following options may be considered:
	+ Use one sensor for control and another sensor for monitoring and reporting
	+ Use two sensors, or their average value, for both monitoring and control
	+ Use dual element sensors for both monitoring and control
**Bioburden Testing (D.7.3)**
When using the bioburden approach, bioburden testing shall be performed at least quarterly.
* The period of monitoring can be extended following a documented risk analysis that considers:
	+ Use of product families
	+ Historical data
	+ Statistical analysis
	+ Manufacturing frequency and product design
**Documentation (D.7.4)**
Upon completion of the product definition, the following shall be documented:
* Equipment specification, including performance and monitoring capabilities
* Redundant sensors used for critical process parameters
**Software Validation (6.3.3)**
The software used to control and/or monitor the sterilization process shall be prepared and validated in accordance with a quality system that provides documented evidence that the software meets its design specification.
**Means of Monitoring and Controlling Process Variables (6.3.4)**
The means of monitoring and controlling the process variables shall be determined and specified.
* Means shall be provided to ensure that failure in a control function does not lead to failure in recording of process variables such that an ineffective process appears effective.
* This may be achieved either by the use of independent systems for control and monitoring or by a cross-check between control and monitoring which identifies any discrepancies.
**Product Requirements for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization**
The purpose of this document is to outline the product requirements for ethylene oxide sterilization as specified in ISO 11135. Compliance with these requirements is essential to ensure the effectiveness and safety of the sterilization process.
**7.1 General - Product Definition**
The product to be sterilized, including its microbiological quality prior to sterilization, shall be defined. This definition shall include:
* The type and quantity of products to be sterilized
* The microbiological quality requirements for the product prior to sterilization
* The manner in which the product is packaged or presented for sterilization
**7.1.1 Purpose of Product Definition**
The purpose of defining the product is to ensure that it meets the required standards for sterilization and safety.
**Determination and Specification of Control Functions (6.3.5)**
Control functions shall be determined and specified to ensure that failure in a control function does not lead to failure in recording of process variables, such that an ineffective process appears effective.
Means to achieve this include:
* The use of independent systems for control and monitoring
* A cross-check between control and monitoring which identifies any discrepancies or indicates a fault
To prevent the release of a sterilization load without having met its required processing parameters, redundant sensors shall be used for many critical process parameters.
Common options for utilizing these redundant sensors include:
* Using one sensor for control and another sensor for monitoring and reporting
* Using two sensors or their average value for both monitoring and control
* Generating an automatic fault condition if the difference between the two sensors exceeds a defined value
**Bioburden Testing (D.7.3.2)**
In health care facilities, bioburden testing shall be performed at least quarterly when using the bioburden approach.
The period of monitoring can be extended following a documented risk assessment.
**Software and Firmware Requirements**
Software and firmware used for ethylene oxide sterilization shall comply with relevant standards, including:
* ISO/TS 11139:2006
* ISO/TS 16775
* IEC 61010-1
* IEC 61010-2-040
**Release of Sterilized Product**
The release of the sterilized product shall be in accordance with the requirements specified in ISO 14937:2009, E.4.2.2.
Compliance with these product requirements is essential to ensure the effectiveness and safety of the sterilization process. Failure to comply may result in ineffective or unsafe sterilization, which can have serious consequences for patient health and safety.
This document has been prepared to be audit-ready, providing a comprehensive guide to the product requirements for ethylene oxide sterilization as specified in ISO 11135.
This document outlines the product requirements for ethylene oxide (EO) sterilization as specified in ISO 11135. Compliance with these requirements is essential to ensure the safety and efficacy of EO sterilized medical devices.
**Measurement and Monitoring Requirements**
1. **Measurement Equipment**
The measurement equipment used for EO sterilization shall meet the following requirements:
	* Be calibrated according to ISO/TS 11139:2006, Sterilization of health care products â€” Vocabulary.
	* Comply with IEC 61010-1, Safety requirements for electrical equipment for measurement, control, and laboratory use â€” Part 1: General requirements.
	* Meet the specific requirements for sterilizers and washer-disinfectors as specified in IEC 61010-2-040.
**Control Requirements**
1. **Process Control**
The EO sterilization process shall be controlled to ensure delivery of the minimum specified product Sterilization Assurance Level (SAL) in all evaluated pieces or sets of equipment.
	* A fractional or half cycle may be performed to demonstrate process capability, provided that microbiological monitoring is included.
2. **Environmental and Personnel Protection**
The potential effect on the environment and personnel shall be assessed, and measures to protect them shall be identified.
	* The assessment, including potential impact and control measures, shall be documented.
3. **EO Emission and Disposal**
Users of EO shall comply with applicable local, national, and international requirements regarding the emission and disposal of EO and its diluents as well as any by-products.
**Process and Equipment Characterization**
1. **General Requirements**
The purpose of process and equipment characterization is to ensure that the sterilization process continues to deliver the required product SAL.
2. **Characterization Activities**
The following activities shall be performed:
	* Description of the EO sterilizing agent delivery system, including sensor characteristics and their locations.
	* Description of instrumentation for monitoring, controlling, and recording the sterilization process, including sensor characteristics and their locations.
	* Identification of fault(s) recognized by the sterilizing equipment.
	* Safety features, including those for personnel and environmental protection.
	* Installation requirements, including specifications for required services and control of emissions.
**Software Validation**
The software used to control and/or monitor the process shall be prepared and validated in accordance with a quality system that provides documented evidence that the software meets its design specification. For further information, refer to ISO 13485.
**Effluent Gas Disposal**
Effluent gas from EO sterilization processes shall be discharged through an EO gas treatment system, such as a catalytic oxidizer, wet acid scrubber, or thermal oxidizer in compliance with local permit requirements or emission control legislation.
**Product and Process Change Control**
To ensure continued process effectiveness, it is necessary to evaluate any changes to the product and packaging, processes, and equipment. A comprehensive product and process change control system is recommended. One parameter commonly monitored to ensure continued ability to sterilize the load is the product bioburden, which shall be monitored according to ISO 11737-1.
**Conclusion**
Compliance with these product requirements for EO sterilization ensures the safety and efficacy of medical devices sterilized using this process. Manufacturers and users of EO sterilization equipment must adhere to these requirements to maintain compliance with regulatory standards.

**Product Definition (D.7)**
The purpose of this activity is to define the product to be sterilized, including its microbiological quality prior to sterilization and packaging details. The product definition involves documentation of essential information about the medical device, such as:
* Purpose: The intended use of the medical device
* Description: A detailed description of the medical device, including its design, materials, and functionality
* Microbiological Quality: The microbiological quality of the product prior to sterilization
* Packaging Details: The manner in which the product is packaged for sterilization
**Control (D.7.1)**
The control requirements for ethylene oxide sterilization are critical to ensure the effective removal of microorganisms from medical devices. To meet these requirements, it is essential to have redundant sensors for many critical process parameters.
The common options for utilizing these redundant sensors include:
* a) Use one sensor for control and another sensor for monitoring and reporting
* b) Use two sensors or their average value for both monitoring and control. This system must generate an automatic fault condition if the difference between the two sensors exceeds a defined value.
* c) Use dual element sensors for both monitoring and control. This system must generate an automatic fault condition if the difference between the two elements exceeds a defined value.
**Control of Nonconforming Product (4.4)**
To ensure compliance with ISO 11135, it is essential to have a robust system in place for controlling nonconforming products. This includes:
* Identification: The identification of nonconforming products
* Documentation: The documentation of nonconforming products, including the reasons for nonconformance and any corrective actions taken
* Corrective Action: The implementation of corrective action to prevent recurrence
**Measurement (4.3)**
To ensure compliance with ISO 11135, it is essential to have a robust system in place for measurement and analysis. This includes:
* Measurement: The measurement of critical process parameters, such as temperature, humidity, and ethylene oxide concentration
* Analysis: The analysis of data from measurement systems to ensure compliance with regulatory requirements
**Importance of Compliance**
Compliance with ISO 11135 is essential to ensure the effective sterilization of medical devices using ethylene oxide. Failure to comply can result in ineffective sterilization, which can compromise patient safety and lead to product recalls.
**Audit-Ready Requirements**
To ensure compliance with ISO 11135, it is essential to have a robust system in place for auditing and verification. This includes:
* Documentation: The documentation of all processes and procedures related to ethylene oxide sterilization
* Training: The training of personnel involved in ethylene oxide sterilization on regulatory requirements and best practices
* Auditing: Regular auditing of the ethylene oxide sterilization process to ensure compliance with regulatory requirements.

* ISO 11135:2014 Ethylene Oxide Sterilization - Validation and Routine Control
* Regulatory Requirements (e.g., FDA, EU MDR)
This section outlines the essential requirements for products undergoing ethylene oxide sterilization, as specified in ISO 11135. Compliance with these requirements is crucial to ensure the safety and effectiveness of medical devices sterilized using this method.
**1. Installation and Operation of Ethylene Oxide Sterilizers**
Ethylene oxide sterilizers shall be installed in a dedicated room (ISO 11135:2014+A1:2019, Clause 5.2). The operating controls for the sterilization equipment shall be mounted outside the room to prevent operators from entering the sterilization area while setting or changing program parameters.
**2. Control of Ethylene Oxide Concentration**
The concentration of ethylene oxide in the sterilizer shall be controlled and monitored to ensure safe and effective sterilization. The operating controls for the sterilizer shall include provisions for measuring the relative proportions of ethylene oxide, air, diluent gas (e.g., CO2), inert gas (e.g., nitrogen), and water vapor in the sterilizer.
**3. Safety Precautions**
To prevent safety and quality issues, caution shall be exercised to ensure that no separation of the ethylene oxide blend can occur during sterilization.
**4. Product Testing for Sterility**
The product test of sterility (PTS) is required to validate the effectiveness of the sterilization process. The number of samples selected for PTS shall not be less than that used for bioburden determination (ISO 11135:2014+A1:2019, Clause E.2.7).
**5. Comparative Resistance Assessment**
If comparative resistance of the internal PCD versus product bioburden has previously been assessed using a fractional cycle of shorter duration than that of the half cycle in E.2.7, and there have been no positive test results from the PTS samples and the bioburden testing demonstrates comparable results (numbers and types), then it is not necessary to perform the PTS for product test samples exposed to a full sterilization cycle.
**6. Validation of Sterilization Process**
The sterilization process shall be validated using a combination of methods, including:
* Endotoxin testing
* Bioburden determination
* Product test of sterility
**7. Reference Standards and Guidelines**
The following standards and guidelines shall be consulted for guidance on ethylene oxide sterilization:
* ANSI/AAMI ST41:1999 (Ethylene oxide sterilization in health care facilities: Safety and effectiveness)
* ANSI/AAMI ST67 (Sterilization medical devices â€” Requirements for products labeled â€˜STERILEâ€™)
* AAMI TIR15 (Physical aspects of ethylene oxide)
* AAMI TIR16 (2009)
Compliance with these product requirements is essential to ensure the safety and effectiveness of medical devices sterilized using ethylene oxide. Failure to comply may result in compromised product quality, reduced shelf life, or even patient harm.
**Audit-Ready Documentation**
To ensure compliance, manufacturers shall maintain accurate records of:
* Installation and operation of ethylene oxide sterilizers
* Control of ethylene oxide concentration
* Product testing for sterility
* Comparative resistance assessment (if applicable)
* Validation of sterilization process
These records shall be readily available for audit purposes.

**118. microbial**

## ðŸ”¹ **Biological Indicator Compliance Requirements**

**Biological Indicator Requirements for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization (ISO 11135)**
**Introduction**
The use of Biological Indicators (BIs) is a critical component of the ethylene oxide sterilization process. BIs are used to verify the effectiveness of the sterilization process and ensure that products are free from viable microorganisms. This guidance outlines the requirements for BIs as specified in ISO 11135.
**Temperature Monitoring**
Temperature monitoring is essential to ensure that the sterilization process is effective. According to Annex C (informative) of ISO 11135, it is recommended to use one temperature sensor per 2.5 mÂ³ during Operational Qualification (OQ) to establish a thermal map of the room or chamber. This will help identify potential hot or cold locations and ensure that monitoring includes more than one plane.
**Relative Humidity (RH) Monitoring**
RH monitoring is also critical to ensure that the sterilization process is effective. According to ISO 11135, RH meters must be in conformance with the specifications established during validation for the specific product(s) in a defined load. Parametric release is based upon a documented review of processing records rather than the testing of biological indicators or Process Control Devices (PCDs). The values and tolerances for both RH and EO concentration may need to be generated after review of a predefined number of routine cycles.
**Biological Indicator Requirements**
BIs must comply with the requirements specified in ISO 11135. BIs are used as part of the routine monitoring and control of loads processed, and their use is justified and recorded. The rationale for the number of runs selected should be documented.
**Chemical Indicators**
Chemical indicators shall not replace biological indicators for product release or be used to support a rationale to release a load parametrically. If parametric release is performed, additional data must be recorded and retained, including:
* Temperature in the chamber from a minimum of two locations throughout the sterilization cycle
* Chamber humidity during conditioning as determined by direct measurement
* EO concentration, determined from direct analysis of chamber atmosphere using analytical methods at defined intervals sufficient to ensure that allowable product EO residuals are met.
**Validation and Requalification**
The validation process must include the deposit of microorganisms for the purposes of patent and regulation. The reference microorganism microbial strain obtained from a recognized culture collection is used in the validation process. Requalification is necessary to confirm the continued acceptability of a specified process, and it should be performed at least annually.
**Importance of Compliance**
Compliance with Biological Indicator requirements is essential to ensure that products are free from viable microorganisms. Failure to comply with these requirements can result in product contamination and compromise patient safety.
**Audit-Ready Checklist**
To ensure compliance with Biological Indicator requirements, the following audit-ready checklist should be used:
* Temperature monitoring: Are temperature sensors used per 2.5 mÂ³ during OQ?
* RH monitoring: Are RH meters in conformance with specifications established during validation?
* BI usage: Are BIs used as part of routine monitoring and control of loads processed?
* Chemical indicators: Are chemical indicators not used to replace biological indicators for product release or support parametric release?
* Additional data recording: Is additional data recorded and retained, including temperature, chamber humidity, and EO concentration?
By following this guidance and using the audit-ready checklist, organizations can ensure compliance with Biological Indicator requirements and maintain the effectiveness of their ethylene oxide sterilization process.
**Biological Indicator Requirements for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization**
The use of a Biological Indicator (BI) is a critical component in ensuring the effectiveness and reliability of an ethylene oxide sterilization process. This document outlines the requirements for the validation, qualification, and control of biological indicators as specified in ISO 11135.
**Validation Requirements**
1. **Requalification Program**: The requalification program shall be conducted annually to ensure that inadvertent process changes have not occurred and to demonstrate that the original validation remains valid.
2. **Acceptable Ranges and Levels of Variability**: The requalification program should define acceptable ranges and levels of variability in performance that are necessary to maintain the validity of the original validation from year to year.
3. **Investigation of Non-Conformity**: In the event of a non-conformity, an investigation shall be initiated to try to determine the root cause(s) of the non-conformity and its impact on the validity of the requalification program.
**Process Qualification (PQ)**
1. **Biological Indicators Used in PQ**: Biological indicators used in PQ shall comply with the applicable clauses of ISO 11138-1:2006.
2. **Chemical Indicators**: Chemical indicators used as part of PQ shall comply with ISO 11140-1 and be used in conjunction with microbiological and physical monitoring.
**Validation Report**
1. **Preparation of Validation Report**: A validation report shall be prepared, including results from incubation of biological indicators.
2. **Review and Approval**: The validation report shall be reviewed and approved by the designated responsible person(s).
3. **Content of Validation Report**: The validation report shall describe or reference specific qualified product, defined load configurations, and the documented specification for the EO sterilization process.
**Release of Product**
1. **Use of Saleable Product in Validation Studies**: If saleable product is used in validation studies, the requirements for release of this product for distribution shall be generated before the start of the validation activities.
2. **Effect on Product and Packaging Functionality**: The effect of repeated exposures to the validation/sterilization processes on product and packaging functionality, and levels of residual ethylene oxide, shall be assessed.
**Training and Competence**
1. **Personnel Training**: Each organization shall establish procedures for identifying training needs and ensure that all personnel are trained to adequately perform their assigned responsibilities.
2. **Management Responsibility**: The management system shall include quality policy, planning, responsibility, authority, and communication, and management review.
**Qualification Requirements**
1. **Product Conformance Criteria**: Product shall be considered as non-conforming and handled in accordance with the applicable clauses of ISO 13485 if one or more of the conformance criteria are not fulfilled.
2. **Investigation of Non-Conformity**: In the event of a positive BI, it is not acceptable to release product based on acceptable results of a product test for sterility.
**Biological Indicator Incubation**
1. **Establishment of Conditions**: The conditions used for recovery of biological indicators in qualification studies, including duration of incubation, shall be established and documented.
2. **Incubation Period**: The incubation period shall take into account the possibility of delayed outgrowth of spores that have been exposed to EO.
**Compliance Importance**
The use of a Biological Indicator is critical in ensuring the effectiveness and reliability of an ethylene oxide sterilization process. Compliance with these requirements is essential to ensure patient safety and prevent harm from contaminated medical devices.
**Audit-Ready Guidance**
This document provides comprehensive guidance on the biological indicator requirements for ethylene oxide sterilization, as specified in ISO 11135. It is intended to be used by organizations implementing an ethylene oxide sterilization process and provides a framework for ensuring compliance with regulatory requirements.
The use of biological indicators (BIs) is a critical component of ethylene oxide sterilization processes. BIs serve as a means to validate the effectiveness of the sterilization process and ensure that products are rendered free from viable microorganisms. This guidance outlines the requirements for the qualification, validation, and operation of BIs in accordance with ISO 11135.
**Qualification of Biological Indicators**
1. **Routine Processing Parameters**: The routine processing parameters that deliver a minimum of 12 Spore Log Reduction (SLR) of the biological indicator shall be established using one of the methods described in A.1.3.
2. **Number of Cycles**: The number of cycles required for qualification is dictated by the method used.
3. **Recovery Conditions**: The conditions used for recovery of BIs in qualification studies shall be established and documented, taking into account the possibility of delayed outgrowth of spores that have been exposed to EO.
4. **Incubation Period**: The incubation period shall be determined based on the guidance provided in ISO 14161.
**Qualification Following Significant Changes**
1. **Significant Changes**: In circumstances where a significant change has occurred, such as changes to product/packaging design or configuration (creating a new "worst-case" condition), process design or equipment/service, qualification of BIs shall be repeated.
2. **Professional Judgment**: In the absence of physical or microbiological qualification requirements, professional judgment can be used where no changes have been made to product, packaging, equipment/services and process, acceptable chamber performance and engineering review, and the routine sterilization process has operated reliably in the intervening period.
1. **Observations of Growth**: Observations of growth from BIs not attributable to failure to meet physical process specifications shall be analyzed; this can lead to a need for process or equipment modifications, and for the PQ to be repeated.
2. **Healthcare Facility Applications**: In healthcare facility applications, external chemical indicators in health care facilities: sterilizer indicator tape, an indicating label or an indicating printed legend should be affixed to or printed on each package assembled by the manufacturer.
**Validation**
1. **Test for Sterility**: A test for sterility technical operation shall be defined in a Pharmacopoeia and performed on product following exposure to a sterilization process.
2. **Usable Chamber Volume**: The usable chamber volume shall be defined as the space within the sterilizer chamber, which is not restricted by fixed or mobile parts and which is available for processing.
**Spore Log Reduction (SLR)**
1. **Overkill Approach**: An overkill approach using a sterilization process that delivers a minimum of 12 SLR to a BI having a resistance equal to or greater than the product bioburden shall be used.
2. **Parametric Release Declaration**: A parametric release declaration that product is sterile, based on records demonstrating that the process parameters were delivered within specified tolerances, shall be made.
**D-Value and Lethality Rate**
1. **D-Value Calculation**: The D-value of the biological indicator (see D.8.6) shall be determined by running the sterilization cycle at graded exposure times, or by exposing graded BI populations to a single sterilization exposure time, and then determining the lethal rate (rate of inactivation through D-value calculations).
2. **Impact of Packaging**: Attention shall be given to the impact of packaging and the removal of EO from products on the lethality rate.
The use of BIs is critical for ensuring that ethylene oxide sterilization processes are effective and reliable. Compliance with these requirements is essential for maintaining the integrity of products and preventing contamination. Manufacturers, healthcare facilities, and regulatory authorities must ensure that BIs are qualified, validated, and operated in accordance with these requirements to maintain compliance with ISO 11135.
**Audit-Ready Documentation**
All documentation related to BI qualification, validation, and operation shall be maintained and made available for audit purposes. This includes records of qualification studies, process parameters, and lethality rate calculations.
**Biological Indicator Requirements for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization - Compliance with ISO 11135**
The use of biological indicators (BIs) is a critical component in ensuring the effectiveness and reliability of ethylene oxide sterilization processes. As per the requirements specified in ISO 11135, BIs must be used to validate the sterilization process and ensure that it meets the desired level of sterility assurance.
**D-Value Calculation**
The D-value is a measure of the resistance of biological indicators to ethylene oxide sterilization. It shall be calculated in accordance with ISO 11737-1 and 11737-2, using a linear regression model as described in ISO 14161:2009. The survivor count can be used to develop a survivor curve and calculate the D-value.
**Fraction-Negative Analysis**
Fraction-negative analysis involves running sterilization cycles where some, but not all, of the biological indicators are inactivated. This includes:
1. **Holcomb-Spearman-Karber (HSK) procedure**: A statistical method for estimating the number of survivors based on the fraction of negative samples.
2. **Lim**: A method for calculating the number of survivors based on the ratio of positive to negative samples.
The SLR is a measure of the reduction in spore population after exposure to ethylene oxide sterilization. It shall be calculated using one of the following methods:
1. **Direct Enumeration**: SLR = log N0 - log Nu, where N0 is the initial population and Nu is the final population.
2. **Fraction-Negative**: SLR = log N0 - log [ln (q/n)], where q is the number of replicate samples tested and n is the number of samples negative for growth.
**Cycle Calculation Approach**
The routine processing parameters that deliver a minimum 12 SLR of the biological indicator shall be established using one of the methods described in A.1.3. The number of cycles is dictated by the method used.
**Recovery Technique Validation**
The adequacy of the recovery technique for BIs exposed to EO gas shall be demonstrated using a short cycle, as specified in ISO 14161:2009. This can also be used to demonstrate the relative resistance of Biological Indicator, PCD and product bioburden.
**Qualification Studies**
The conditions used for recovery of biological indicators in qualification studies shall be established and documented. The incubation period and temperature shall be specified in detail within an approved document.
**Sterility Assurance Level (SAL)**
The log reduction of the internal PCD can be used to calculate the sterility assurance level achieved for the product bioburden with the most resistance to the sterilization process. If this is the case, then the Spore Log Reduction (SLR) data developed in a lethality study for the BI can be used to demonstrate the effectiveness of the process for the product.
The use of biological indicators is critical in ensuring the effectiveness and reliability of ethylene oxide sterilization processes. Compliance with these requirements is essential to ensure that products are sterile and safe for use.
All documentation related to the use of biological indicators, including qualification studies, recovery technique validation, and cycle calculation approaches, shall be maintained in a format that is easily accessible and auditable.
By following these guidelines, manufacturers can ensure compliance with ISO 11135 requirements for biological indicators and maintain the highest level of sterility assurance for their products.
The use of a biological indicator (BI) is essential to ensure the effectiveness and reliability of ethylene oxide (EO) sterilization processes. This document outlines the requirements for the selection, qualification, and validation of BIs in accordance with ISO 11135.
**1. Spore Log Reduction (SLR)**
The SLR is a critical parameter used to demonstrate the effectiveness of the EO sterilization process. The user shall compare the spore log reduction achieved by the product bioburden with the resistance of the BI. If the product bioburden has the most resistance to the sterilization process, then the SLR data developed in a lethality study for the BI can be used to demonstrate the effectiveness of the process.
**1.1 Calculation of Spore Log Reduction**
The SLR is calculated using one of two methods:
*   For Direct Enumeration: SLR = log N0 âˆ’ log Nu
    *   Where:
        *   N0 is the initial population
        *   Nu is the final population
*   For Fraction Negative: SLR = log N0 â€“ log [ln (q/n)]
        *   q is the number of recoveries
        *   n is the total number of samples
**2. Biological Indicator Requirements**
The BI shall be qualified and validated to ensure its effectiveness in demonstrating the sterility assurance level (SAL) achieved by the EO sterilization process.
**2.1 Resistance of Biological Indicator**
The resistance of the internal PCD shall be demonstrated by running the sterilization cycle at graded exposure times or by exposing graded BI populations to a single sterilization exposure time, and then determining the lethal rate using D-value calculations.
**2.2 Cycle Calculation Approach**
The routine processing parameters that deliver minimally a 12 SLR of the biological indicator shall be established using one of the methods described in A.1.3. The number of cycles is dictated by the method used.
**2.3 Recovery Technique for Biological Indicators**
A fractional cycle of short duration from which BI survivors can be recovered shall also be run to demonstrate the adequacy of the recovery technique for BIs exposed to EO gas.
**3. D-Value Calculations**
The D-value is a critical parameter used to calculate the lethality delivered by the EO sterilization process.
*   The D-value represents the time required to reduce the population of microorganisms by 90% when exposed to the specified sterilization process.
*   The D-value can be calculated using one of two commonly used methods:
    *   Enumeration: consists of an enumeration or physical count of the surviving microorganisms
    *   Survivor Curve Method: uses a survivor curve generated from lethality studies
The use of a biological indicator is essential to ensure the effectiveness and reliability of EO sterilization processes. Failure to comply with these requirements may result in inadequate sterilization, leading to contamination and potential harm to patients.
All documentation related to the qualification and validation of BIs shall be maintained on file and made available for audit purposes. This includes:
*   Spore log reduction calculations
*   Biological indicator resistance data
*   Cycle calculation approach
*   Recovery technique for biological indicators
*   D-value calculations
By following these guidelines, users can ensure the effectiveness and reliability of their EO sterilization processes and maintain compliance with regulatory requirements.
**Biological Indicators for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization**
Biological indicators (BIs) are critical components of ethylene oxide (EO) sterilization processes, serving as a means to validate the effectiveness of the process in achieving sterility. This document provides comprehensive guidance on the requirements and best practices for implementing biological indicators in EO sterilization.
**D-Value Requirements**
The D-value is a measure of the resistance of a biological indicator to a given sterilization process. According to ISO 11135, the D-value shall be determined using data from selected papers (Pflug I.J., ed.). The D-value calculation shall take into account the effects of EtO BIER-Vessel Operating Precision on D-value calculations, as described by Mosley G.A. and Gillis J.R.
**SLR Method**
The Sterilization Load Ratio (SLR) method is a commonly used approach to demonstrate total inactivation of the 10^6 challenge BIs at a half-cycle exposure time. When this exposure time is doubled, a minimum of 12 SLR shall be delivered during EO exposure. This approach ensures that the process delivers considerably more than 12 SLR.
**Cycle Calculation**
The cycle calculation method involves exposing internal Process Control Devices (PCDs) to the experimental cycle, removing the challenge, and testing for survivors. This testing can be conducted using a suitable biological indicator test system.
A biological indicator shall consist of viable microorganisms providing a defined resistance to a specified sterilization process. The performance of the sterilization process used for a particular sterilization load shall be documented, including:
1. Confirmation that the data recorded during routine processing meet the sterilization process specification.
2. Confirmation of no growth of the test organism from any biological indicator (if used).
**Documentation and Validation**
The following documentation is required to validate the use of biological indicators in EO sterilization:
1. The criteria for validation shall include confirmation that the data recorded during routine processing meet the sterilization process specification, as well as confirmation of no growth of the test organism from any biological indicator.
2. Formal release of the load from sterilization may require results from other tests (e.g., EO residuals, endotoxin, physical testing) before product can enter the distribution chain.
**Annex A: Determination of Lethal Rate**
The lethal rate of the sterilization process can be determined using a biological indicator/bioburden approach. This method combines knowledge of the resistance of a biological indicator to a given sterilization process with knowledge of the bioburden population and resistance to establish the sterilization process parameters (sterilization cycle exposure time).
**Incubation Period**
The incubation period for biological indicators in qualification studies shall be established and documented. The incubation period shall take into account the possibility of delayed outgrowth of spores that have been exposed to EO.
**Recovery of Biological Indicators**
The conditions used for recovery of biological indicators in qualification studies shall be established and documented. Further guidance on the biological indicator incubation times can be found in ISO 14161.
**Resistance of Product Bioburden**
The resistance of the product bioburden shall be shown to be such that, total inactivation time of the product bioburden is less than the total inactivation time of the product BI (internal PCD).
**Procedure for Creating a Challenge**
A challenge to the sterilization process shall be created using a suitable biological indicator test system. The conditions used for recovery of biological indicators in qualification studies shall be established and documented.
The use of biological indicators is critical in ensuring the effectiveness of EO sterilization processes. Compliance with these requirements ensures that products are sterile and safe for use, reducing the risk of contamination and associated health risks.
**Audit-Ready Requirements**
To ensure compliance with ISO 11135, the following audit-ready requirements shall be met:
1. Documentation of biological indicator performance and validation.
3. Formal release of the load from sterilization requires results from other tests (e.g., EO residuals, endotoxin, physical testing) before product can enter the distribution chain.
By following these guidelines, manufacturers and healthcare facilities can ensure that their EO sterilization processes meet the required standards for biological indicators, ensuring the safety and sterility of products.
**Biological Indicator Requirements for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization - Compliance Guidance**
The use of biological indicators (BIs) is a critical component in ensuring the effectiveness of ethylene oxide sterilization processes. This compliance guidance outlines the requirements and best practices for implementing BIs in accordance with ISO 11135:2014+A1:2019.
**Importance of Biological Indicators**
Biological indicators are used to validate the efficacy of ethylene oxide sterilization processes by demonstrating the lethality rate of microorganisms exposed to the process. The use of BIs is essential for ensuring that products are sterile and safe for use.
**Configuration of Biological Indicators**
The configuration of biological indicators, especially in mixed product loads, shall meet the requirements specified in ISO 11138-1 and ISO 14161. A minimum number of samples shall be used to ensure representative results. The internal process control device (PCD) shall provide an equal or greater challenge than that of the bioburden located in the most inaccessible portion of the product.
**Validation of Biological Indicators**
The validation of biological indicators shall be performed in accordance with the following procedures:
1. **Cochran Procedure (SMCP)**: The Cochran procedure involves exposing graded BI populations to a single sterilization exposure time and determining the lethal rate through D-value calculations.
2. **Survival-Curve Method (EN)**: This method involves running the sterilization cycle at graded exposure times or exposing graded BI populations to a single sterilization exposure time, followed by determination of the lethal rate.
**Minimum Exposure Time**
The minimum exposure time for the sterilization process shall be determined through a series of validation runs. The specified exposure time for the sterilization process shall be at least double this minimum time.
**Fractional Cycle**
The route of calculation for determining the exposure time shall take into account the lethality rate, population and relative resistance of the bioburden, packaging, and removal of EO from the PCD. Guidance on this approach can be found in ISO 14161.
**Biological Indicator Incubation Times**
Further guidance on biological indicator incubation times can be found in ISO 14161.
**Procedure for Creating a Challenge to the Sterilization Process**
A challenge to the sterilization process, PCD, comprising a known number of microorganisms with known resistance to EO, shall be created by placing biological indicators in the product or inoculating product at locations where sterilizing conditions are most difficult.
**Release from Validation**
Release from validation is based upon a documented review of processing records rather than the testing of biological indicators or PCDs. The values and tolerances for both RH and EO concentration might need to be generated after review of a predefined number of routine cycles.
**Monitoring and Control**
Biological indicators might be used as part of the routine monitoring and control of loads processed during this evaluation period.
**Documentation and Justification**
The rationale for the number of runs selected shall be justified and recorded. This can be influenced by uniformity of the load, existing data, seasonal variations or frequency of sterilization.
**Compliance Checklist**
To ensure compliance with the requirements outlined in this guidance, the following checklist should be used:
1. **Configuration of Biological Indicators**: Ensure that biological indicators meet the requirements specified in ISO 11138-1 and ISO 14161.
2. **Validation of Biological Indicators**: Perform validation runs using both Cochran procedure (SMCP) and survival-curve method (EN).
3. **Minimum Exposure Time**: Determine the minimum exposure time for the sterilization process through a series of validation runs.
4. **Fractional Cycle**: Run a fractional cycle to demonstrate the adequacy of the recovery technique for BIs exposed to EO gas.
5. **Cycle Calculation Approach**: Use the route of calculation specified in ISO 14161 to determine the exposure time.
6. **Biological Indicator Incubation Times**: Follow the guidance outlined in ISO 14161 for biological indicator incubation times.
7. **Resistance of Product Bioburden**: Demonstrate that the total inactivation time of the product bioburden is less than the total inactivation time of the product BI (internal PCD).
8. **Procedure for Creating a Challenge to the Sterilization Process**: Create a challenge to the sterilization process, PCD, comprising a known number of microorganisms with known resistance to EO.
9. **Release from Validation**: Document
**Biological Indicators for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization - Compliance Guidance**
The use of biological indicators (BIs) is a critical component in ensuring the effectiveness and reliability of ethylene oxide (EO) sterilization processes. As specified in ISO 11135, BIs are used to validate the sterility assurance level (SAL) of medical devices processed using EO. This guidance provides an overview of the requirements for Biological Indicators as per ISO 11135, emphasizing their importance and compliance significance.
According to ISO 11135, a BI sample set exposed at zero time should be subjected to all stages of the experimental cycle prior to sterilant injection (D.14.1.3). The incubation period for BIs is provided in ISO 14161:2009, Section 12.3 (D.14.1.4).
To demonstrate the appropriateness of a BI relative to bioburden inactivation time, a test of sterility can be performed either before or during process definition using a fractional-cycle of the appropriate exposure time (D.14.2). This ensures that the BI is suitable for validating the SAL of medical devices processed using EO.
**Microbial Strains and Culture Collections**
For the purpose of validation, microbial strains must be obtained from recognized culture collections, as defined in ISO/TS 11139:2006 (Definitions 2.38-2.40). These collections provide a standardized source for microorganisms used in BI development and testing.
**Sterilization Validation Process**
A sterilization validated process is essential to render medical devices free from viable microorganisms (3.47). The nature of microbial inactivation is exponential, and thus the survival of a microorganism on an individual item can be expressed in terms of probability (Note 1 to entry).
**Probability of Microbial Survival**
The probability of microbial survival can never be reduced to zero, even with a very low number (3.46). Therefore, it is essential to understand that a SAL of 10-6 provides greater assurance of sterility than an SAL of 10-3.
**Material Effects and EO Compositions**
EO has been comprehensively documented in literature, providing knowledge on the manner in which process variables affect microbial inactivation (5.4). However, reference to these general studies is not required by this International Standard.
The effects of EO on a wide variety of materials used to manufacture medical devices have also been extensively documented and are valuable for those designing and developing medical devices that will be processed using EO.
**Developmental Chamber Studies**
When using a developmental chamber for process definition, consideration should be given to establishing the relationship between data from developmental chamber studies and production chamber data (D.9.4.2.4). This is particularly important when developing microbial inactivation curves, which may not always be possible in production chambers due to size constraints and injection/removal times.
**Product Families and Processing Categories**
Medical devices can be grouped into product families based on commonality within a processing category (e.g., intravenous sets and syringes). All products within this category should present an equivalent or lesser challenge to the sterilization process compared with the worst-case product, representative member, or internal PCD.
The use of BIs is critical in ensuring compliance with regulatory requirements for EO sterilization. Failure to meet these requirements can result in non-compliance and potential risks to patient safety.
This guidance provides a comprehensive overview of the Biological Indicator requirements as per ISO 11135, emphasizing their importance and compliance significance. It serves as an audit-ready resource for organizations seeking to ensure compliance with regulatory requirements for EO sterilization.
By following this guidance, medical device manufacturers can ensure that their BIs are suitable for validating the SAL of medical devices processed using EO, thereby ensuring patient safety and regulatory compliance.
The use of a Biological Indicator (BI) is essential in ethylene oxide sterilization processes to ensure that the product has been effectively sterilized. This document outlines the requirements and guidelines for the implementation of BIs in accordance with ISO 11135.
**Qualification and Validation**
11.1 **Conformance Criteria**: The BI shall be qualified before use in a sterilization process. This qualification involves demonstrating that the BI is capable of detecting the lethality of the sterilization cycle.
11.2 **Non-Conforming Product**: If one or more conformance criteria are not fulfilled, the product shall be considered non-conforming and handled in accordance with applicable clauses of ISO 13485.
**BI Requirements**
12.1 **Consistency over Time**: The BI used for validation studies shall be consistent over time, and its resistance to bioburden shall be shown to be equal to or less resistant than the resistance of the biological indicator.
12.2 **Resistance Demonstration**: The resistance of the internal Process Control Device (PCD) shall be demonstrated by running the sterilization cycle at graded exposure times or exposing graded BI populations to a single sterilization exposure time, followed by determination of the lethal rate through D-value calculations.
**BI/PCD Selection**
13.1 **Selection Criteria**: The selection of BIs and PCDs for use in ethylene oxide sterilization shall depend on:
a) Microbiological qualification method chosen (see Annex A or Annex B);
b) Product volume;
c) Type of chamber (developmental vs. production).
**Approach 1: Fractional Cycle**
14.1 **Fractional Cycle**: In this approach, a test of sterility of the product and PCD is performed following a fractional cycle. The results of this study shall provide a means of lethality comparison using survival data from the tests of sterility for the product and PCD.
**Approach 2: Direct Enumeration**
15.1 **Direct Enumeration**: In cases where an indication exists that sufficient bioburden data are available, direct enumeration methods and/or fraction-negative methods (see ISO 14161) can be used to demonstrate the lethality challenge of the bioburden and PCD.
**Approach 3: Fractional Cycle with Direct Enumeration**
16.1 **Fractional Cycle with Direct Enumeration**: This approach can be applied in cases where:
a) The product bioburden challenge is equal to or greater than the challenge of the BI within the PCD;
b) The product bioburden contains highly resistant microorganisms; or
c) A BI with a lower population than required by ISO 11138-2:2006, 9.3 is used in the PCD.
The use of BIs and PCDs in ethylene oxide sterilization processes is critical to ensure that products are effectively sterilized and meet regulatory requirements. Compliance with these guidelines is essential for maintaining a high level of sterility assurance level (SAL) and preventing product contamination.
To ensure compliance, the following audit-ready requirements shall be met:
* A qualified BI shall be used in each sterilization process.
* The resistance of the internal PCD shall be demonstrated through D-value calculations or direct enumeration methods.
* The lethality challenge of the bioburden and PCD shall be based on direct enumeration methods and/or fraction-negative methods (see ISO 14161).
* A fractional cycle test of sterility for the product and PCD shall be performed to demonstrate lethality comparison.
By following these guidelines, manufacturers can ensure that their ethylene oxide sterilization processes meet regulatory requirements and maintain a high level of sterility assurance level (SAL).
The determination of lethal rate of the sterilization process is a critical aspect of ethylene oxide (EO) sterilization. This compliance guidance focuses on the requirements for biological indicators (BIs) as specified in ISO 11135, providing clear and authoritative information to ensure compliance with regulatory standards.
Biological indicators are used to validate the effectiveness of the EO sterilization process. They provide a means to determine the lethality challenge of the sterilization process and ensure that it delivers a Sterilization Assurance Level (SAL) of 10^-3 or less for all products.
**Requirements for Biological Indicators**
The following requirements apply to biological indicators used in EO sterilization:
1. **Sample Set Exposure**: The sample set exposed at zero time should be exposed to all stages of the experimental cycle prior to sterilant injection.
2. **Number of Biological Indicators/PCDs**: When using the Stumbo-Murphy-Cochran procedure and the Overkill Cycle Calculation approach, a minimum of 10 biological indicators (BIs)/product configurations devices (PCDs) is recommended.
3. **Lethality Challenge**: The lethality challenge of the external PCD should not be less than 20% of the lethality challenge of the internal PCD.
**Determination of Lethal Rate**
The lethal rate of the sterilization process can be determined using either the biological indicator/bioburden approach or the overkill approach. The combined biological indicator/bioburden approach is based on the use of a resistant BI or other internal PCD with a population that is equal to or greater than that of the bioburden.
**Guidance on Annex A - Determination of Lethal Rate**
Annex A provides guidance on the determination of lethal rate using the biological indicator/bioburden approach. This annex should be used in conjunction with Clauses 8 and 9 for further information regarding the use of this approach.
**Guidance on Annex B - Conservative Determination of Lethal Rate**
Annex B provides guidance on a conservative determination of lethal rate using the overkill approach. When using the cycle calculation approach, see also Clause D.13.1.1.
**Validation and Verification**
To ensure compliance with regulatory standards, the following steps should be taken:
1. **Establish a New Sterilization Process**: Establish a new sterilization process for the candidate product.
2. **Validate the Master Product**: Validate that the candidate product is equivalent to the currently validated master product.
3. **Determine Lethal Rate**: Determine the lethal rate of the sterilization process using either the biological indicator/bioburden approach or the overkill approach.
**Annex E - Single Batch Release**
Single batch release is a method used to validate the effectiveness of a single batch of products. This annex provides guidance on the requirements for single batch release.
**Conclusion**
Biological indicators play a critical role in validating the effectiveness of EO sterilization processes. Compliance with regulatory standards requires careful consideration of the requirements outlined in this compliance guidance. By following these guidelines, manufacturers can ensure that their biological indicators meet the necessary standards and provide accurate results to validate the lethality challenge of the sterilization process.

* ISO 14161:2009 Sterilization of medical instruments - Information to be provided by the manufacturer for the processing of medical instruments

To ensure compliance with regulatory standards, manufacturers should maintain records and documentation on the following:
1. **Biological Indicator/Bioburden Data**: Records of biological indicator/bioburden data used to determine lethal rate.
2. **Lethality Challenge**: Documentation of lethality challenge for external PCDs and internal PCDs.
3. **Validation and Verification**: Records of validation and verification activities, including single batch release.
4. **Training and Competency**: Documentation of training and competency programs for personnel involved in EO sterilization.
By maintaining accurate records and documentation, manufacturers can ensure compliance with regulatory standards and provide evidence of their commitment to quality and safety.
**Biological Indicator Requirements for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization - ISO 11135**
**Introduction:**
The use of a biological indicator (BI) is an essential aspect of ethylene oxide sterilization, providing assurance that the process has achieved its intended microbial state. This document outlines the requirements for Biological Indicators as specified in ISO 11135.
**1. General Requirements**
* The BI shall be used to demonstrate the effectiveness of the sterilization process.
* The BI population size shall be equal to or greater than that of the bioburden.
* Sufficient bioburden data from the bioburden monitoring program must be available to support the use of a resistant BI.
**2. Conservative Determination of Lethal Rate (Overkill Approach)**
* The overkill approach, as described in Annex B and Clause 8, shall be used to determine the lethal rate of the sterilization process.
* When using the cycle calculation approach, refer to D.13.1.1 for further guidance.
**3. General Safety and Performance Requirements**
* This standard addresses only those aspects related to the attainment of a specific microbial state by ethylene oxide treatment.
* Design and packaging for maintenance of sterility or another specific microbial state during transportation and storage are not covered.
* Aspects of manufacture other than those related to attainment of sterility or another specific microbial state by ethylene oxide are not covered.
**4. Validation and Routine Control**
* This standard provides requirements for the development, validation, and routine control of a sterilization process using ethylene oxide for medical devices.
* The sterilized medical device shall be safe and perform as intended after treatment.
**5. Process Control**
* All factors influencing process control, including physical characteristics and manufacturer performance claims (e.g., accuracy, repeatability, size, and model), shall be kept on file.
* Process control logic or software documentation necessary to support validation, including:
	+ Control system layout
	+ Control logic diagrams
	+ Application software (computerized measurement and control systems) such as program listings, flow charts, ladder logic diagrams where applicable, and strategy diagrams
**6. Compliance Importance:**
Compliance with the Biological Indicator requirements specified in ISO 11135 is essential to ensure that medical devices are safe and perform as intended after ethylene oxide sterilization.
**7. Audit-Ready Requirements:**
* The BI population size shall be documented.
* Sufficient bioburden data from the bioburden monitoring program must be available.
* Process control logic or software documentation necessary to support validation shall be kept on file.
By following these requirements, manufacturers can ensure that their Biological Indicators are used effectively and that their ethylene oxide sterilization processes meet the standards specified in ISO 11135.

**Monitoring Biological Indicators**
When monitoring biological indicators, it is essential to follow established procedures to prevent any potential risks associated with inadequate EO processing. If the results of the biological indicator suggest inadequate EO processing, the contents of the package should not be used. The complete unused package, including load identification and the chemical indicator, should be returned to the processing department for appropriate follow-up.
The results of physical monitoring, chemical indicators elsewhere in the load, and biological monitoring should be reviewed to reach a conclusion as to whether the entire load should be recalled or not. Records of this review should be retained. A single non-responsive or inconclusive indicator should not be considered evidence that the entire load is non-sterile.

To ensure the safety, quality, and performance of products following sterilization, it is essential to verify that the product and its packaging meet specified requirements for sterilization using defined process parameters. Design control is a critical aspect addressed in ISO 14971. If multiple sterilization cycles are permitted, the effects of such processing on the product and its packaging should be evaluated.

The accuracy and reliability of instrumentation used to control and monitor the sterilization process shall be verified periodically in accordance with documented procedures.

**Process Control and Validation**
The development, validation, and routine control of a sterilization process can involve multiple parties with separate responsibilities. It is essential to establish clear procedures outlining the roles and responsibilities of each party involved in the process. Process equivalence can be established through analysis of process data combined with microbiological evaluation.

This method does not include the use of biological indicators.

2. **Note**: An electronic sensor measures EO gas concentration at only one sample site, whereas the calculated EO gas concentration represents the mean EO gas concentration within the space (volume) available for EO gas molecules to reside.
