**Biological Indicators - Requirements and Guidelines**
The use of Biological Indicators (BIs) is a critical component in the validation and verification of ethylene oxide (EO) sterilization processes, as specified in ISO 11135. The purpose of this document is to provide guidance on the requirements for BIs, including concentration, exposure time, and recovery techniques.
**Concentration**
The calculated EO gas concentration within the chamber shall be determined using a validated method, taking into account factors such as sensor dynamic performance characteristics, placement of the sensor, and potential stratification within the chamber. The calculated concentration represents the mean EO gas concentration within the space available for EO gas molecules to reside.
To ensure accurate measurement, an equilibration time may be necessary at the start of the EO dwell phase of the cycle to allow the chamber concentration to stabilize as the EO gas is distributed throughout the chamber and penetrates into void spaces in the load.
**Exposure Time**
The exposure time for BIs shall be determined using one or more of the following approaches:
a) **Half-cycle approach**: A total of three consecutive experiments resulting in total inactivation of the biological indicators (with a population of not less than 10^6 and, where appropriate, placed within a PCD) shall be performed to confirm the minimum exposure time. The specified exposure time for the sterilization process shall be at least double this minimum time.
b) **Fractional cycle approach**: A fractional cycle of short duration from which BI survivors can be recovered shall also be run to demonstrate the adequacy of the recovery technique for BIs exposed to EO gas.
**Duration**
The incubation period for recovering biological indicators in qualification studies, including duration of incubation, shall be established and documented. The incubation period shall take into account the possibility of delayed outgrowth of spores that have been exposed to EO.
Refer to ISO 14161 for additional information on biological indicator incubation times.
**Recovery Techniques**
After time-graded exposures, BIs shall be recovered using a validated method, taking into account factors such as packaging and removal of EO from the PCD. Guidance on this approach can be found in ISO 14161.
The use of Biological Indicators is critical for ensuring the effectiveness of ethylene oxide sterilization processes. Compliance with these requirements ensures that BIs are accurately measured, exposed to sufficient time, and recovered using validated methods, thereby verifying the efficacy of the sterilization process.
To ensure compliance with ISO 11135, the following documentation shall be maintained:
* Calculated EO gas concentration within the chamber
* Equilibration time used at the start of the EO dwell phase of the cycle
* Exposure time determined using one or more of the approaches outlined above
* Incubation period for recovering biological indicators in qualification studies
* Validation records for recovery techniques
By following these guidelines, organizations can ensure that their Biological Indicators are accurately measured and validated, thereby verifying the efficacy of their ethylene oxide sterilization processes.
The use of biological indicators (BIs) is a critical component in the validation and verification of ethylene oxide sterilization processes. This document provides guidelines on the requirements for BIs, as specified in ISO 11135:2014+A1:2019.
### A. General Requirements
* Biological indicators shall be used to confirm the minimum exposure time for the sterilization process.
* The specified exposure time for the sterilization process shall be at least double the minimum time confirmed by the BI.
### B. Exposure Time Confirmation
To confirm admission of ethylene oxide (EO) to the chamber, one or more of the following methods may be used:
1. Mass of EO used
2. Direct measurement of the concentration of EO in the sterilizer chamber
3. Volume of EO used
4. EO-injection time
5. Inert gas injection, if used
6. Exposure time
7. Time taken to evacuate the chamber
8. Time and pressure changes during post-exposure flushing
9. Time, temperature, pressure changes (if any) during aeration
### C. Biological Indicator/Bioburden Approach
This approach combines knowledge of the resistance of a biological indicator to a given sterilization process with knowledge of the bioburden population and resistance to establish the sterilization process parameters.
* The product bioburden levels shall be demonstrated to be relatively consistent over time.
* The resistance of the bioburden shall be shown to be equal to, or less resistant than the resistance of the biological indicator (see D.8.6).
### D. Exposure Time Methods
#### Half Cycle Approach
This method is commonly used due to its relative ease of use and conservative Sterilization Assurance Level (SAL) obtained.
* The half-cycle exposure time shall be used to demonstrate total inactivation of 10^6 challenge BIs.
* When this exposure time is doubled, a minimum of 12 SALs shall be delivered during EO exposure.
#### Cycle Calculation
This method consists of exposing internal Process Control Devices (PCDs) to the experimental cycle, removing the challenge and testing for survivors.
### E. Validation Requirements
The appropriateness of the BI relative to the bioburden inactivation time can be demonstrated by a test of sterility, either before or during process definition using a fractional-cycle of the appropriate exposure time.
* The internal PCDs placed within the product sterile barrier system shall provide at least as great a challenge to sterilization process as the product they represent.
* The challenge of the internal PCD to the sterilization process can be used to demonstrate the effectiveness of the process for the product.
### F. Cycle Time Validation
The minimum cycle time derived from this approach is not, by itself, adequate to validate the sterilization process. Demonstration of the ability to maintain process parameters within defined limits during the proposed full cycle is necessary.
The use of biological indicators is a critical component in ensuring the effectiveness and safety of ethylene oxide sterilization processes. Compliance with these requirements is essential for maintaining regulatory compliance and ensuring patient safety.
To ensure compliance, the following audit-ready checklist should be used:
* Biological indicators are used to confirm the minimum exposure time for the sterilization process.
* The specified exposure time for the sterilization process is at least double the minimum time confirmed by the BI.
* One or more of the methods listed in B. Exposure Time Confirmation are used to confirm admission of EO to the chamber.
* The product bioburden levels are demonstrated to be relatively consistent over time.
* The resistance of the bioburden is shown to be equal to, or less resistant than the resistance of the biological indicator (see D.8.6).
* The half-cycle exposure time is used to demonstrate total inactivation of 10^6 challenge BIs.
* A minimum of 12 SALs are delivered during EO exposure when the half-cycle exposure time is doubled.
* Internal PCDs placed within the product sterile barrier system provide at least as great a challenge to sterilization process as the product they represent.
* The challenge of the internal PCD to the sterilization process is used to demonstrate the effectiveness of the process for the product.
By following these guidelines and using this audit-ready checklist, organizations can ensure compliance with the biological indicator requirements specified in ISO 11135:2014+A1:2019.
The use of a biological indicator (BI) is an essential aspect of ethylene oxide (EO) sterilization processes. It provides assurance that the process has achieved its intended purpose, i.e., the elimination or inactivation of microorganisms. Compliance with the requirements outlined in this section is crucial to ensure the efficacy and safety of EO sterilized products.
### 5.2 Sterilizing Agent Specification
The sterilizing agent specification for ethylene oxide shall include, if appropriate, conditions of storage to maintain the EO within its specified limits for the duration of the stated shelf life.
#### Storage Conditions
To ensure the effectiveness and stability of the EO, it is essential to store it under conditions that prevent degradation. The storage conditions shall be specified in accordance with the manufacturer's recommendations.
### 5.3 Microbicidal Effectiveness
Microbicidal effectiveness data shall be developed if it is proposed to use the EO outside of the range of compositions that are within the limits specified in ISO 11135:2014+A1:2019.
#### Scope and Limitations
The microbicidal effectiveness data shall be used to validate the sterilization process for specific product types, packaging configurations, or equipment designs. The data shall not be extrapolated beyond the scope of the validation study.
### Validation Studies
Validation studies undertaken in test or prototype equipment shall demonstrate the efficacy of the EO sterilization process. These studies shall be conducted in accordance with ISO 11135:2014+A1:2019 and shall include:
*   **Duration**: The duration of the validation study shall be sufficient to ensure that the EO has achieved its intended purpose.
*   **Sterilizing Agent Specification**: The sterilizing agent specification shall be maintained within its specified limits throughout the duration of the study.
### Compliance Importance
Compliance with the biological indicator requirements outlined in this section is essential to ensure the efficacy and safety of EO sterilized products. Failure to comply may result in inadequate sterilization, which can lead to product contamination, recalls, or even patient harm.
To ensure compliance with the biological indicator requirements for ethylene oxide sterilization:
1.  Verify that the sterilizing agent specification includes conditions of storage to maintain the EO within its specified limits.
2.  Ensure that microbicidal effectiveness data are developed for specific product types, packaging configurations, or equipment designs.
3.  Conduct validation studies in test or prototype equipment to demonstrate the efficacy of the EO sterilization process.
4.  Maintain records of sterilizing agent specifications, storage conditions, and validation study results.
By following this guidance, organizations can ensure compliance with the biological indicator requirements for ethylene oxide sterilization and maintain confidence in their processes.

The organization shall specify procedures for development, validation, routine control, and product release from sterilization (ISO 2014 â€“ All rights reserved BS EN ISO 11135:2014+A1:2019).

The conclusion should include or reference any results from additional tests performed to supplement the existing validation study, as well as further testing performed for confirmation/qualification for routine release of product from the existing validated cycle.

* **Control of Non-Conforming Product**: Procedures for control of non-conforming product and corrective action are specified in ISO 13485:2003, 8.3 and 8.5.2, respectively.

**Records/Documents Requirements for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization - Compliance with ISO 11135**
Maintaining accurate and complete records is essential for ensuring compliance with the requirements of ISO 11135 for ethylene oxide sterilization. This document provides guidance on the Records/Documents requirements specified in the standard.
**1. Lot Identification Information**
Lot identification information enables personnel to retrieve items sterilized in a specific cycle in the event of a recall and to trace problems to their source (D.4.3.3). It is essential that lot control identifiers include the following information:
* Sterilizer ID or code
* Date of sterilization
* Cycle number (i.e., the cycle run of the day or sterilizer)
* Identity of the person who assembled the pack
**2. Calibration of Monitoring and Measuring Instrumentation**
A system complying with the applicable clause(s) of ISO 13485 or ISO 10012 shall be specified for the calibration of all equipment, including instrumentation for test purposes, used in meeting the requirements of this International Standard (4.3.3). The procedures for control of non-conforming product and corrective action are specified in ISO 13485:2003, 8.3 and 8.5.2, respectively.
**3. Control of Non-Conforming Product**
Procedures for control of product designated as nonconforming and for correction, corrective action, and preventive action shall be specified (4.4). These procedures shall comply with the applicable clauses of ISO 13485.
**4. Sterilizing Agent Characterization**
The purpose of this activity is to define the sterilizing agent characterization process (5.1 General).
**5. Calibration and Maintenance of Equipment**
A documented program for calibration of instrumentation used to control and monitor a sterilization process is necessary to ensure that the process continues to deliver product with the required SAL and performance characteristics (D.12.1.2). The maintenance of equipment, including periodic equivalence reviews, shall be conducted in accordance with D.12.5.10.
**6. Change Control**
A change control process shall be implemented to review changes to each piece of equipment, the manufacturing process, the product load, and the sterilization process to ensure that these changes do not compromise the overall determination of equivalence (D.12.5.9). If any process fails the periodic equivalence review, then it should be removed from the equivalence list and requalified on its own.
**7. Documentation**
All decisions related to the outcome of the analysis determining whether candidate equipment can be declared equivalent to the existing equipment shall be documented (D.12.5.10).
**8. Review and Approval of Documents and Records**
Documents and records required by this International Standard shall be reviewed and approved by designated personnel (4.1.2). Procedures for development, validation, routine control, and product release from sterilization shall be specified (4.1.1).
Maintaining accurate and complete records is essential for ensuring compliance with the requirements of ISO 11135. Failure to comply with these requirements may result in non-conforming products being released into the market, which can have serious consequences for patient safety.
**Audit-Ready Requirements**
To ensure compliance with the Records/Documents requirements specified in ISO 11135, the following audit-ready requirements shall be met:
* Lot identification information is accurately recorded and includes the required information.
* Calibration of monitoring and measuring instrumentation is conducted in accordance with the applicable clause(s) of ISO 13485 or ISO 10012.
* Procedures for control of non-conforming product are specified and comply with the applicable clauses of ISO 13485.
* Sterilizing agent characterization process is defined and documented.
* Equipment calibration and maintenance programs are implemented and documented.
* Change control process is implemented to review changes to each piece of equipment, the manufacturing process, the product load, and the sterilization process.
* Documents and records required by this International Standard are reviewed and approved by designated personnel.
By following these guidelines, organizations can ensure compliance with the Records/Documents requirements specified in ISO 11135 and maintain accurate and complete records that support the safe and effective use of ethylene oxide sterilized products.
**Records/Documents Requirements for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization - ISO 11135**
Effective record-keeping and documentation are essential components of a robust quality management system in ethylene oxide sterilization. The purpose of these requirements is to ensure that all records and documents related to the sterilization process are accurate, complete, and readily accessible for audit and review purposes.
**Control and Validation Records**
The organization shall maintain control and validation records for the sterilization process, including:
1. **Confirmation or Qualification for Routine Release**: Further testing performed for confirmation or qualification of routine release of product from an existing validated cycle, such as residual testing or functional testing on the first three lots.
2. **Approval by Sterilization Specialist**: Approval by the sterilization specialist and other individuals required by normal change control or process documentation control practices within the organization.
3. **Sterilizer Operating Procedures and Specifications**: A list of applicable sterilizer operating procedures and specifications issued or changed to authorize use of the candidate equipment for routine processing of product.
**Parametric Release Records**
When parametric release is used, the organization shall maintain records that include:
1. **Formal Review of Process Documentation**: A formal review of the process documentation by a designated individual (or a validated automated process) to verify and document that physical cycle variables are within tolerances defined in the sterilization process specification.
2. **EO Concentration Profile Assessment**: If parametric release is used, the EO concentration profile for the entire gas dwell phase shall be assessed to determine how the gas concentration changes over the phase.
**Concentration Monitoring Records**
The organization shall maintain records of concentration monitoring, including:
1. **Sensor Placement**: The sensor should be placed within the sterile barrier system or amongst unit packages to achieve optimal concentration monitoring.
2. **Temperature Sensor Placement**: Temperature sensors within the sterilization load should be placed in locations that are most likely to experience the greatest temperature variation, taking into account hot and cold spots.
**Electronic Records**
Routine release of a product following sterilization can be based on a review of electronic records in lieu of paper records. Required signatures can also be made electronically.
Maintaining accurate and complete records is essential for ensuring compliance with ISO 11135 requirements and regulatory expectations. Inadequate record-keeping can lead to non-compliance, product contamination, or even recalls. Therefore, it is crucial that organizations prioritize record-keeping and documentation as a critical component of their quality management system.
**Audit Readiness**
These records shall be readily accessible for audit and review purposes, ensuring that the organization is prepared to demonstrate compliance with ISO 11135 requirements.

## ðŸ”¹ **Safety Precaution Compliance Requirements**

**Safety Precautions for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization**
**Introduction**
Compliance with the safety precautions outlined in ISO 11135 is essential to ensure a safe working environment during ethylene oxide sterilization processes. Failure to adhere to these requirements can result in serious health risks and damage to equipment.
**Temperature Monitoring (Clause 7.5)**
The load temperature shall be taken into account in relation to the chamber temperature to ensure adequate load temperature in the routine process. To achieve this, the following conditions shall apply:
- When sensors are used in the sterilization chamber:
  - The temperature and humidity sensors shall be intrinsically safe.
  - Alternatively, they shall be of an explosion-proof design.
**Sensor Compatibility (Clause 7.5)**
Temperature and humidity sensors used in conjunction with ethylene oxide or potentially flammable sterilant mixtures shall meet the following requirements:
- They shall be functionally compatible with ethylene oxide and any diluent gases.
- This compatibility is essential to prevent potential hazards during the sterilization process.
**Implementation and Verification**
To ensure compliance, organizations shall implement and verify the following procedures:
1.  Conduct regular checks on temperature and humidity sensors to ensure they meet the specified requirements.
2.  Verify that sensors are compatible with ethylene oxide and any diluent gases used in the sterilization process.
3.  Maintain accurate records of sensor performance and compatibility testing.
**Compliance Importance**
Adherence to these safety precautions is crucial for maintaining a safe working environment during ethylene oxide sterilization processes. Non-compliance can result in serious health risks, damage to equipment, and potential liability issues.
By implementing the required safety precautions outlined in ISO 11135, organizations can ensure a safe and compliant sterilization process that meets regulatory requirements.
**Audit Readiness**
This guidance is designed to be comprehensive and audit-ready. Organizations shall maintain accurate records of sensor performance and compatibility testing, as well as regular checks on temperature and humidity sensors, to demonstrate compliance with the specified safety precautions.

## ðŸ”¹ **Monitoring Compliance Requirements**

**Monitoring Requirements for Ethylene Oxide (EO) Sterilization**
**Introduction**
Monitoring is a critical aspect of EO sterilization, ensuring that products are properly sterilized and meet the required standards for safety. This document outlines the monitoring requirements as specified in ISO 11135.
**Temperature Monitoring**
Temperature monitoring is essential to ensure that products are exposed to the correct temperature conditions during EO sterilization. The following guidelines apply:
* Temperature-measuring devices (PCDs) shall be placed within the product case and evenly distributed throughout the sterilization load.
* PCDs should include locations where sterilization conditions are most difficult to achieve, such as corners or crevices.
* For palletized loads, top and bottom of the pallets shall also be included in temperature monitoring to assess potential stratification within the chamber.
* Sample numbers for temperature monitoring can be found in Table C.3.
**Heat Transfer and Penetration**
To demonstrate adequate penetration of EO, humidity, and heat into products, a PCD should be chosen for routine monitoring and validation of the EO sterilization process. The resistance of the PCD to EO shall be shown to be equal to or greater than the resistance of the bioburden of product to be sterilized at the most difficult-to-sterilize location on the product.
**Validation of Sterilization Process**
The establishment of the sterilization process shall comply with ISO 11138-2:2006, Clause 5 and 9.5. The validation process shall:
* Be shown to be at least as resistant to EO as is the bioburden of product to be sterilized.
* Use a PCD that presents a challenge to the sterilization process equivalent or greater than the natural bioburden at the most difficult-to-sterilize location within the product.
**Routine Monitoring and Control**
Routine monitoring and control shall include:
* Temperature of products entering the preconditioning area, which should be at or above the minimum temperature specified or meet defined conditions of storage.
* Heat transfer and penetration, as described above.
* Chamber temperature, recorded from two separate monitoring locations.
* Load configuration, including weights and densities of items.
**Process Specification**
A process specification shall be established for routine processing based on the documentation generated during validation. This specification shall include:
* Process parameters and their tolerances.
* Criteria for designating EO-processed product as conforming product and approved for release.
**Importance of Compliance**
Monitoring is essential to ensure that products are properly sterilized and meet the required standards for safety. Failure to comply with monitoring requirements can result in inadequate sterilization, compromising patient safety and potentially leading to serious health consequences.
**Audit Readiness**
This document provides comprehensive guidance on monitoring requirements for EO sterilization, ensuring compliance with ISO 11135. Regular audits shall be conducted to verify that monitoring procedures are in place and being followed correctly.
By following these guidelines, organizations can ensure that their EO sterilization processes meet the required standards for safety and quality.
**Monitoring Requirements for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization**
**Compliance Importance:**
Proper monitoring of the ethylene oxide (EO) sterilization process is essential to ensure that products are effectively sterilized and meet the required standards. This includes demonstrating compliance with ISO 11135, which specifies the requirements for EO sterilization.
**Monitoring Process Specification:**
The monitoring process specification shall include:
1. **Validation:** The validation of the sterilization process shall demonstrate that the process is capable of achieving the desired level of sterility.
2. **Routine Monitoring and Control:** Routine monitoring and control are essential to ensure that the validated sterilization process is consistently delivered to the product.
**Routine Monitoring and Control (10.1):**
The purpose of routine monitoring and control is to demonstrate that the validated and specified sterilization process has been delivered to the product.
**Data Recording and Retention:**
Data shall be recorded and retained for each sterilization cycle to demonstrate that the sterilization process specification has been met. These data shall include at least:
1. **Process Parameters:** The process parameters, such as temperature, humidity, and EO concentration.
2. **Product Information:** The product information, including the type of product, batch number, and date of manufacture.
3. **Sterilization Cycle Data:** The sterilization cycle data, including the duration of the cycle and any deviations from the standard cycle.
**Process Challenge Devices (PCDs):**
The appropriateness of the PCD used for process definition, validation or routine monitoring and control shall be determined. The PCD shall present a challenge to the sterilization process that is equivalent or greater than the challenge presented by the natural bioburden at the most difficult to sterilize location within the product.
**Placement of PCDs:**
PCDs should be placed within the product case and evenly distributed in the sterilization load, but distribution should include those locations where sterilization conditions are the most difficult to achieve. The locations used should include those selected for temperature monitoring.
**Concurrent Exposure(s):**
The equivalence of internal versus external PCDs can be assessed using concurrent exposure(s) in a fractional cycle(s). The resulting data can be used for:
1. **Making Decisions:** Making decisions about which internal PCD is appropriate to validate the sterilization process.
2. **Evaluating Candidate Designs:** Evaluating candidate designs for external PCDs (i.e., for routine monitoring of the process).
3. **Assessing Equivalence:** Assessing the equivalence of new or modified products for adoption into a validated sterilization process.
4. **Deciding on Master Product:** Deciding if a new or modified product or internal PCD should become the master product for a product family or processing group.
**Sample Numbers:**
For guidance on sample numbers, see Table C.3.
**Developmental Chamber:**
If a developmental chamber was used during validation, it shall be demonstrated that the results obtained from this chamber are equivalent to those obtained from a production-scale chamber.
By following these monitoring requirements, organizations can ensure compliance with ISO 11135 and demonstrate that their EO sterilization process is effective in achieving the desired level of sterility.
**Monitoring Requirements for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization (ISO 11135)**
**Importance of Monitoring**
Effective monitoring is essential to ensure the quality and safety of ethylene oxide sterilized products. Compliance with ISO 11135 monitoring requirements is crucial to demonstrate the adequacy of penetration of EO, humidity, and heat into products, thereby ensuring the elimination of bioburden.
**Monitoring Objectives**
The objectives of monitoring for ethylene oxide sterilization are:
1. To verify the resistance of product components to EO;
2. To ensure adequate penetration of EO, humidity, and heat into products; and
3. To validate the effectiveness of the EO sterilization process.
**Selection of Product Challenge Devices (PCDs)**
To demonstrate compliance with monitoring requirements, a PCD shall be chosen for routine monitoring and validation of the EO sterilization process. The resistance of the PCD to EO shall be shown to be equal to or greater than the resistance of the bioburden of product to be sterilized at the most difficult to sterilize location on the product.
**Monitoring Requirements**
The following requirements shall be met for monitoring:
1. **Product Characteristics**
	* The different parts of both the product and material;
	* Weights and densities of items; and
	* Load configuration, especially for a mixed product load.
2. **Healthcare Considerations**
	* A PCD shall be chosen for routine monitoring and validation of the EO sterilization process.
3. **Resistance to EO**
	* The resistance of the PCD to EO shall be shown to be equal to or greater than the resistance of the bioburden of product to be sterilized at the most difficult to sterilize location on the product.
**Compliance with ISO 11135**
To ensure compliance with ISO 11135, manufacturers and contract sterilizers must implement monitoring procedures that meet these requirements. Regular audits and reviews shall be conducted to verify compliance with these monitoring requirements.
**Audit-Ready Checklist**
To facilitate audit-readiness, the following checklist is provided:
1. Has a PCD been chosen for routine monitoring and validation of the EO sterilization process?
2. Is the resistance of the PCD to EO equal to or greater than the resistance of the bioburden of product to be sterilized at the most difficult to sterilize location on the product?
3. Are product characteristics (different parts, weights, densities, and load configuration) monitored and documented?
By implementing these monitoring requirements, manufacturers and contract sterilizers can ensure compliance with ISO 11135 and demonstrate the quality and safety of ethylene oxide sterilized products.

## ðŸ”¹ **Acceptance Criteria Compliance Requirements**

**Acceptance Criteria for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization - Compliance with ISO 11135**
**Introduction**
Compliance with the acceptance criteria outlined in this document is essential to ensure that ethylene oxide sterilization processes meet the required standards for product safety and sterility. The purpose of this guidance is to provide a comprehensive overview of the acceptance criteria requirements specified in ISO 11135, ensuring that organizations implementing EO sterilization processes are aware of their responsibilities and obligations.
**Acceptance Criteria for Sterilization Process Validation**
To validate an ethylene oxide sterilization process, it shall be demonstrated that the process consistently produces product meeting the required sterility assurance level (SAL). This shall be achieved by showing that the product sterilized in the validated process meets predetermined specifications and quality characteristics related to product functionality and safety.
**Acceptance Criteria for Product Quality**
The acceptance criteria for product quality shall include:
1. **Product Functionality**: The product shall retain its intended functionality after sterilization.
2. **Stability**: The product shall remain stable throughout the sterilization cycle and subsequent storage conditions.
3. **Biocompatibility**: The product shall comply with specified biocompatibility requirements.
4. **Package Integrity**: The packaging material shall maintain its integrity during and after sterilization.
**Acceptance Criteria for Sterilization Process Parameters**
The following process parameters shall be monitored and controlled to ensure compliance with the acceptance criteria:
1. **Temperature**: The temperature at the end of conditioning and sterilization load temperature during EO exposure shall be equivalent or greater than the minimum values achieved in the half cycle.
2. **Humidity**: The sterilization load humidity at the end of conditioning and sterilization load temperature during EO exposure shall be equivalent or greater than the minimum values achieved in the half cycle.
3. **Vacuum Depth and Rate of Evacuation**: The vacuum depth and rate of evacuation (âˆ†P/time) at selected times during the cycle shall meet specified limits.
4. **Humidification Time and Steam Injection Rate**: The humidification time and steam injection rate (âˆ†P/time) shall meet specified limits.
5. **EO Injection Temperature and Rate**: The EO injection temperature and rate (âˆ†P/time) shall meet specified limits.
6. **Amount of EO Used**: The amount of EO used (weight, concentration, or pressure) shall be within specified limits.
7. **Air or Nitrogen Injection Rate**: The air or nitrogen injection rate (âˆ†P/time) shall meet specified limits.
**Acceptance Criteria for Data Analysis**
The data generated from process monitoring and control shall be analyzed to indicate that the processes are or are not equivalent in their ability to meet existing process parameter limits and any additional acceptance criteria. This analysis shall be performed by a sterilization specialist(s).
**Documentation Requirements**
A written document (e.g., protocol) defining the testing procedures and acceptance criteria for validation of the sterilization process shall be prepared prior to initiation of testing. This document shall be reviewed by a sterilization specialist(s).
**Compliance Importance**
Compliance with the acceptance criteria outlined in this guidance is essential to ensure that ethylene oxide sterilization processes meet the required standards for product safety and sterility. Failure to comply with these requirements may result in compromised product quality, reduced effectiveness of the sterilization process, or even product recalls.
By following this guidance, organizations can ensure that their ethylene oxide sterilization processes are compliant with ISO 11135 and maintain the highest standards of product safety and sterility.

## ðŸ”¹ **Storage & Distribution Compliance Requirements**

**Storage and Distribution Requirements for Ethylene Oxide Sterilization**
**Compliance Importance:**
Proper storage and distribution of ethylene oxide sterilized products are critical to ensure their quality, safety, and efficacy. Non-compliance with these requirements can lead to product contamination, reduced shelf life, or even patient harm.
**Storage Requirements (D.12.5.11.3)**
The design of the candidate product should be carefully reviewed for any changes or differences that could present greater obstacles to ethylene oxide (EO) penetration than the existing product or packaging configuration device (PCD). This includes evaluating:
1. **Product Design Changes**: Longer lumens, added closures, increased number of mated surfaces, or higher product density may impact EO penetration.
2. **Original Product Functionality Testing**: Review the product design against original testing to ensure changes do not compromise product functionality.
**Qualification Requirements (D.12.5.11.3)**
To qualify a candidate product for ethylene oxide sterilization, the following conditions must be met:
1. **Representative Challenge Process**: The EO process used for qualification should constitute a representative challenge to the product and its packaging system.
2. **Documentation**: Address how the challenge process differs from the nominal process, and demonstrate that these parameters are acceptable for product acceptance.
3. **Product Qualification**: Evaluate the candidate product and its packaging to determine the effect on product EO residual levels.
**Spore Log Reduction (D.5.3)**
When using ethylene oxide gas mixtures with carbon dioxide, nitrogen, or other inert gas blends, consider the following:
1. **EO Molecular Diffusion Rates**: EO molecular diffusion rates into polymer materials can be affected by the volume percent of EO gas molecules within the sterilant.
2. **Storage Conditions and Shelf Life**: Store in accordance with the EO manufacturer's recommendations and all applicable regulations.
**Parametric Release (D.11)**
When using parametric release, consider the following:
1. **Mean EO Gas Concentration**: Values obtained by calculating the mean EO gas concentration can differ considerably from direct measured values due to factors such as:
	* Selective absorption and adsorption of EO in the load.
	* Volume taken up by the load.
	* Potential stratification within the chamber.
**Monitoring Requirements (D.11)**
To ensure compliance, implement routine monitoring and control measures:
1. **Physical Monitoring**: Regularly review physical cycle variables to verify they are within tolerances defined in the sterilization process documentation.
2. **Review and Approval of Validation**: Conduct regular reviews and approvals of validation documents to ensure ongoing compliance.
**Control Requirements (D.11)**
To maintain control over the sterilization process, implement:
1. **Routine Monitoring and Control**: Regularly review and document physical cycle variables to ensure they remain within tolerances.
2. **Product Release from Sterilization**: Confirm product release through a formal review of process documentation by a designated individual or automated process.
**Gas Concentration Requirements (D.11)**
When using ethylene oxide gas mixtures, consider the following:
By adhering to these storage, qualification, spore log reduction, parametric release, monitoring, control, and gas concentration requirements, you can ensure the quality, safety, and efficacy of ethylene oxide sterilized products.
**ISO 11135 Compliance Guidance: Storage and Distribution Requirements**
**Introduction**
Proper storage and distribution of ethylene oxide (EO)-sterilized products are critical to maintaining product quality, ensuring customer safety, and upholding the integrity of the sterilization process. This guidance outlines the essential requirements for Storage and Distribution as specified in ISO 11135.
**1. Exposure Conditions**
The sterilization cycle must be conducted under controlled conditions, including:
*   **Exposure Time**: The exposure time during the sterilization cycle shall be roughed out to ensure adequate processing.
*   **Chamber Humidity**: Chamber humidity during conditioning shall be determined by direct measurement.
*   **EO Concentration**: EO concentration shall be determined from direct analysis of chamber atmosphere using analytical methods at defined intervals sufficient to verify the required conditions throughout the exposure time.
**2. Product Release**
To ensure conformance with the sterilization process, the following criteria must be documented:
### 2.1 Criteria for Designating Conformance
The criteria for designating conformance of the sterilization process used for a particular sterilization load shall include:
*   **Confirmation of Recorded Data**: Confirmation that the data recorded during routine processing meet the sterilization process requirements.
*   **Documentation of Sterilization Process**: Documentation of the sterilization process, including any deviations or adjustments made.
**3. Storage and Distribution Requirements**
To maintain product quality and ensure customer safety, the following storage and distribution requirements must be met:
### 3.1 Temperature Control
Products shall be stored at a temperature between 2Â°C and 8Â°C (36Â°F to 46Â°F).
### 3.2 Humidity Control
Products shall be stored in an environment with a relative humidity of not less than 60%.
### 3.3 Packaging Integrity
Packaging materials used for storage and distribution must be compatible with the sterilized product and maintain their integrity throughout the process.
**4. Transportation**
Products shall be transported in a manner that prevents damage, contamination, or exposure to extreme temperatures or humidity levels.
**5. Record Keeping**
Accurate records of storage, handling, and transportation procedures shall be maintained for a minimum of 2 years from the date of product release.
**Conclusion**
Proper Storage and Distribution are critical components of the EO sterilization process. Compliance with these requirements ensures that products meet quality and safety standards, protecting customers and upholding the integrity of the sterilization process.
By following this guidance, organizations can ensure they meet the necessary Storage and Distribution requirements as specified in ISO 11135, maintaining their reputation for quality and compliance.
